Question 1hard

Which of the following best describes the fundamental process involved in measuring any physical quantity?

  1. Comparing it with a certain basic, arbitrarily chosen, internationally accepted reference standard called a unit.
  2. Estimating its value based on prior knowledge and experience.
  3. Using a sophisticated instrument to determine its exact magnitude.
  4. Counting the number of times a standard object fits into the quantity.
Show answer

Answer: Comparing it with a certain basic, arbitrarily chosen, internationally accepted reference standard called a unit.

The measurement of any physical quantity fundamentally involves comparing it to a predefined, universally accepted reference standard, which is known as a unit. This comparison allows for consistent and reproducible measurements across different contexts.

Question 2hard

If the period of oscillation of a simple pendulum is reported as 1.62 s, which digit is considered 'uncertain' and how does it affect the significant figures?

  1. The digit '1' is uncertain, resulting in one significant figure.
  2. The digit '6' is uncertain, resulting in two significant figures.
  3. The digit '2' is uncertain, resulting in three significant figures.
  4. All digits are certain, resulting in three significant figures.
Show answer

Answer: The digit '2' is uncertain, resulting in three significant figures.

In a measurement like 1.62 s, the digits '1' and '6' are considered reliable or certain. The last digit, '2', is the first uncertain digit. Its inclusion indicates the precision of the measurement, and thus, the measurement has three significant figures (1, 6, and 2).

Question 3hard

What is the primary rule for maintaining accuracy when performing arithmetic operations with measured values having a limited number of significant figures?

  1. The result should always have more significant figures than any of the original measured values.
  2. The result should be rounded to the nearest whole number.
  3. The result must reflect the uncertainties in the original measured values and cannot be more accurate than the least accurate original measurement.
  4. The result should have the same number of significant figures as the most accurate original measurement.
Show answer

Answer: The result must reflect the uncertainties in the original measured values and cannot be more accurate than the least accurate original measurement.

When performing calculations with measured values, the accuracy of the result is limited by the least precise measurement. Therefore, the final result should not have more significant figures than the original data with the least number of significant figures, ensuring it reflects the inherent uncertainties.

Question 4hard

Why is it recommended to retain one more significant figure in intermediate results of a multi-step computation?

  1. To make the calculations simpler and faster.
  2. To ensure the final answer is always an integer.
  3. To avoid the accumulation of rounding errors and prevent significant deviation from the accurate final result.
  4. To match the number of significant figures of the most precise measurement in the calculation.
Show answer

Answer: To avoid the accumulation of rounding errors and prevent significant deviation from the accurate final result.

Retaining one extra significant figure in intermediate steps (often called 'guard digit') helps to minimize the impact of rounding errors. Premature rounding at each step can compound these errors, leading to a final result that is less accurate than it should be.

Question 5hard

What dimensional characteristic must the arguments of special functions like trigonometric, logarithmic, and exponential functions always possess?

  1. They must be expressed in SI units.
  2. They must be dimensionless.
  3. They must have the dimension of length.
  4. They must have the dimension of time.
Show answer

Answer: They must be dimensionless.

For mathematical consistency and physical validity, the arguments of special functions such as sin(θ), log(x), or e^y must always be dimensionless. This ensures that the function's output is also dimensionless or has a consistent dimension, regardless of the units used for the input quantities.

Question 6hard

What is a 'system of units' defined as?

  1. A collection of only fundamental (base) units.
  2. A complete set of units, encompassing both fundamental (base) units and derived units.
  3. A set of units used exclusively for measuring length, mass, and time.
  4. Any arbitrary collection of units used in scientific measurements.
Show answer

Answer: A complete set of units, encompassing both fundamental (base) units and derived units.

A 'system of units' refers to a comprehensive and coherent collection that includes both the fundamental (or base) units (like meter, kilogram, second) and all the derived units (like Newton, Joule, Watt) that are formed from these base units. The SI system is a prime example.

Question 7hard

One mole of an ideal gas at STP occupies 22.4 L. If the atomic volume of a mole of hydrogen is approximately 3.156 × 10⁻⁷ m³, what is the approximate ratio of molar volume to atomic volume, and why is it so large?

  1. Approximately 7.1 × 10², because gas molecules are very small.
  2. Approximately 7.1 × 10⁴, because gas molecules are widely separated with much empty space.
  3. Approximately 7.1 × 10⁻², because gas molecules are tightly packed.
  4. Approximately 7.1 × 10⁻⁴, because the atomic volume is much larger than molar volume.
Show answer

Answer: Approximately 7.1 × 10⁴, because gas molecules are widely separated with much empty space.

Molar volume = 22.4 L = 22.4 × 10⁻³ m³. Atomic volume ≈ 3.156 × 10⁻⁷ m³. Ratio = (22.4 × 10⁻³ m³) / (3.156 × 10⁻⁷ m³) ≈ 7.098 × 10⁴. This large ratio indicates that in a gas, molecules are widely separated, and the vast majority of the volume is empty space between them, unlike in liquids or solids.

Question 8hard

How does differential calculus help determine instantaneous velocity when the position of an object is known as a function of time?

  1. By calculating the average velocity over a very small time interval.
  2. By finding the integral of the position function with respect to time.
  3. By taking the derivative of the position function with respect to time.
  4. By simply dividing the total displacement by the total time taken.
Show answer

Answer: By taking the derivative of the position function with respect to time.

In kinematics, if the position (x) of an object is given as a function of time (t), the instantaneous velocity (v) at any given moment can be precisely determined by taking the first derivative of the position function with respect to time, i.e., v = dx/dt.

Question 9hard

In real-world physical situations, why are graphs of position, velocity, and acceleration typically smooth without sharp kinks?

  1. Physical quantities are always discrete, leading to smooth transitions.
  2. Changes in physical quantities are always continuous, making the functions differentiable at all points.
  3. Idealized models always assume smooth graphs for simplicity.
  4. Measurement errors always smooth out any sharp changes in real data.
Show answer

Answer: Changes in physical quantities are always continuous, making the functions differentiable at all points.

In physics, real-world changes in physical quantities like position, velocity, and acceleration are continuous. This continuity implies that the functions representing these quantities are differentiable at all points, which graphically translates to smooth curves without abrupt changes or sharp kinks. Abrupt changes would imply infinite acceleration or velocity, which is physically impossible.

Question 10hard

Galileo's law of odd numbers states that for a body falling from rest, the distances traversed in successive equal time intervals are in the ratio 1:3:5:.... Which of the following equations is fundamental to deriving this law?

  1. v = u + at
  2. v² = u² + 2as
  3. s = ut + ½at²
  4. s = (u+v)/2 * t
Show answer

Answer: s = ut + ½at²

Galileo's law of odd numbers for a body falling from rest (initial velocity u=0) is derived using the equation of motion s = ut + ½at². Since u=0 and a=g (acceleration due to gravity), the distance fallen is y = ½gt². By calculating the distance fallen at times τ, 2τ, 3τ, etc., and then finding the difference in distances for successive equal time intervals, the 1:3:5 ratio emerges.

Question 11hard

Under what condition can negative acceleration lead to an increase in an object's speed?

  1. When the object is moving in the positive direction and acceleration is negative.
  2. When the object is moving in the negative direction and acceleration is positive.
  3. When both the object's velocity and acceleration are in the negative direction.
  4. Negative acceleration always decreases speed, never increases it.
Show answer

Answer: When both the object's velocity and acceleration are in the negative direction.

Speed is the magnitude of velocity. Negative acceleration means the acceleration vector points in the negative direction. If an object is already moving in the negative direction (negative velocity), and the acceleration is also in the negative direction, then the acceleration is acting in the same direction as the velocity. This causes the magnitude of the velocity (speed) to increase. For example, a car moving left (negative velocity) and braking hard (negative acceleration, assuming positive is right) will slow down. But if it's moving left and the engine is pushing it harder left (negative acceleration), its speed will increase.

Question 12hard

A police van moving at 30 km/h fires a bullet with a muzzle speed of 150 m/s at a thief's car speeding away at 192 km/h in the same direction. What is the speed with which the bullet hits the thief's car?

  1. 105 m/s
  2. 150 m/s
  3. 158.33 m/s
  4. 53.33 m/s
Show answer

Answer: 105 m/s

First, convert all speeds to m/s: Police van speed = 30 km/h = 30 * (5/18) m/s ≈ 8.33 m/s. Thief's car speed = 192 km/h = 192 * (5/18) m/s ≈ 53.33 m/s. Muzzle speed of bullet = 150 m/s. The speed of the bullet with respect to the ground is the muzzle speed plus the van's speed (since it's fired in the same direction): 150 m/s + 8.33 m/s = 158.33 m/s. The speed with which the bullet hits the thief's car is the relative speed between the bullet and the car: |158.33 m/s - 53.33 m/s| = 105 m/s.

Question 13hard

What are the two essential conditions for two vectors, A and B, to be considered equal?

  1. They must have the same magnitude and be parallel.
  2. They must have the same direction and be collinear.
  3. They must have the same magnitude and the same direction.
  4. They must originate from the same point and have the same magnitude.
Show answer

Answer: They must have the same magnitude and the same direction.

For two vectors to be considered equal, they must satisfy two fundamental conditions: they must have precisely the same magnitude (length) and they must point in exactly the same direction. If either of these conditions is not met, the vectors are not equal.

Question 14hard

If rain is falling vertically with velocity 'v_r' and wind is blowing horizontally with velocity 'v_w', what is the magnitude of the resultant velocity of the rain as observed by someone on the ground?

  1. v_r + v_w
  2. |v_r - v_w|
  3. √(v_r² + v_w²)
  4. √(v_r² - v_w²)
Show answer

Answer: √(v_r² + v_w²)

Since the vertical velocity of rain and the horizontal velocity of wind are perpendicular to each other, their resultant velocity can be found using the Pythagorean theorem. The magnitude of the resultant velocity (R) is given by R = √(v_r² + v_w²).

Question 15hard

The statement 'each component of the resultant vector R is the sum of the corresponding components of A and B' is significant because it implies:

  1. Vector addition is always commutative.
  2. Vector addition can be simplified into scalar additions along perpendicular axes.
  3. The magnitude of the resultant vector is always the sum of the magnitudes of individual vectors.
  4. Vectors can only be added if they are collinear.
Show answer

Answer: Vector addition can be simplified into scalar additions along perpendicular axes.

This statement highlights the power of vector resolution. By breaking down vectors into their components along mutually perpendicular axes (like x, y, and z), the complex process of vector addition is reduced to simple algebraic (scalar) addition of corresponding components. This simplifies calculations significantly, as the effect of the resultant vector along any axis is simply the sum of the individual vector's effects along that same axis.

Question 16hard

How is instantaneous acceleration determined graphically from an object's motion?

  1. By calculating the slope of the position-time graph at a specific point.
  2. By finding the area under the velocity-time graph.
  3. By considering the average acceleration over increasingly smaller time intervals (Δt → 0).
  4. By measuring the tangent to the acceleration-time graph.
Show answer

Answer: By considering the average acceleration over increasingly smaller time intervals (Δt → 0).

Instantaneous acceleration is defined as the limit of the average acceleration as the time interval (Δt) approaches zero. Graphically, this means we look at the average acceleration over progressively smaller time intervals. As Δt approaches zero, the average acceleration converges to the instantaneous acceleration, and its direction is the direction of the change in velocity (Δv) in that limit. This is equivalent to finding the slope of the tangent to the velocity-time graph at that instant.

Question 17hard

For a projectile launched with initial velocity v₀ at an angle θ₀ with the horizontal, what is the formula for the time taken to reach its maximum height (tₘ)?

  1. tₘ = (v₀ cos θ₀) / g
  2. tₘ = (v₀ sin θ₀) / g
  3. tₘ = (2v₀ sin θ₀) / g
  4. tₘ = (v₀² sin² θ₀) / (2g)
Show answer

Answer: tₘ = (v₀ sin θ₀) / g

At the maximum height of a projectile's trajectory, the vertical component of its velocity (vₚ) becomes zero. Using the first equation of motion for vertical motion, vₚ = uₚ + at, where uₚ = v₀ sin θ₀ and a = -g. So, 0 = v₀ sin θ₀ - gtₘ. Rearranging this gives tₘ = (v₀ sin θ₀) / g.

Question 18hard

In the derivation of centripetal acceleration for uniform circular motion, which geometric property is crucial for relating the change in position and velocity vectors?

  1. The Pythagorean theorem applied to the position vectors.
  2. The similarity between the triangle formed by position vectors and the triangle formed by velocity vectors.
  3. The law of cosines applied to the velocity vectors.
  4. The fact that the magnitude of velocity remains constant.
Show answer

Answer: The similarity between the triangle formed by position vectors and the triangle formed by velocity vectors.

The key insight is that the triangle formed by the position vectors (r, r', Δr) and the triangle formed by the velocity vectors (v, v', Δv) are similar. This similarity arises because the velocity vector is always perpendicular to the position vector, meaning the angle between r and r' is equal to the angle between v and v'. This allows us to set up a ratio of corresponding sides, which is fundamental in deriving the magnitude of centripetal acceleration.

Question 19hard

Which of the following expressions correctly defines the instantaneous velocity (v) of an object at time t?

  1. v = Δr / Δt
  2. v = lim (Ιt→∞) (Δr / Δt)
  3. v = lim (Δt→0) (Δr / Δt)
  4. v = dr / dt, where dr is the total displacement.
Show answer

Answer: v = lim (Δt→0) (Δr / Δt)

Instantaneous velocity is defined as the limiting value of the average velocity as the time interval Δt approaches zero. This is mathematically represented as the derivative of the position vector (r) with respect to time (t), i.e., v = dr/dt. Option 2 is incorrect because the limit should be as Δt approaches zero, not infinity. Option 0 represents average velocity, not instantaneous velocity. Option 3 is partially correct but the limit definition is more precise.

Question 20hard

Consider three vectors A, B, and C that do not lie in the same plane. Can these three vectors add up to give a null vector (zero resultant)?

  1. Yes, if their magnitudes are appropriately chosen.
  2. Yes, if they form a closed triangle in 3D space.
  3. No, because their resultant (A+B) would not be coplanar with C.
  4. No, unless one of the vectors is a null vector itself.
Show answer

Answer: No, because their resultant (A+B) would not be coplanar with C.

For three vectors A, B, and C to sum to a null vector (A + B + C = 0), it implies that A + B = -C. The vector (A + B) is the resultant of A and B, and it must lie in the plane formed by A and B. For A + B to be equal to -C, vector C must also lie in the same plane as A and B. Therefore, if the three vectors are not coplanar, their sum cannot be a null vector. This statement is true.

Question 21hard

According to the NCERT Class 11 Physics text, what was the primary focus of the chapter preceding the discussion on laws of motion?

  1. Understanding the forces causing motion.
  2. Describing the motion of a particle in space quantitatively.
  3. Analyzing energy transformations in physical systems.
  4. Studying the properties of matter at rest.
Show answer

Answer: Describing the motion of a particle in space quantitatively.

The chapter 'Motion in a Plane' (or 'Kinematics') typically precedes 'Laws of Motion' in the NCERT Class 11 Physics syllabus. The primary concern of kinematics is to describe motion (position, velocity, acceleration) without considering the forces causing it. Therefore, describing the motion of a particle in space quantitatively is the correct answer.

Question 22hard

What was Galileo's significant conclusion regarding the states of rest and uniform linear motion?

  1. Rest is a natural state, while uniform linear motion requires a continuous force.
  2. Both states are equivalent and imply no net force acting on the body.
  3. Uniform linear motion is a state of constant acceleration.
  4. Rest is a state of zero velocity, while uniform linear motion is a state of zero acceleration.
Show answer

Answer: Both states are equivalent and imply no net force acting on the body.

Galileo's experiments and reasoning led to the profound insight that the state of rest and the state of uniform linear motion (constant velocity) are fundamentally equivalent. In both cases, there is no net external force acting on the body. This concept laid the groundwork for Newton's First Law of Motion (Law of Inertia).

Question 23hard

When a bus starts moving moderately, why is a passenger able to accelerate along with it without slipping?

  1. Due to the passenger's inertia, which keeps them moving forward.
  2. The normal force from the floor pushes the passenger forward.
  3. The static friction between the passenger's feet and the bus floor provides the necessary force.
  4. Air resistance pushes the passenger along with the bus.
Show answer

Answer: The static friction between the passenger's feet and the bus floor provides the necessary force.

For the passenger to accelerate with the bus, a force must act on them in the direction of the bus's acceleration. This force is provided by the static friction between the passenger's feet and the bus floor. If the acceleration is moderate, this static friction is sufficient to prevent slipping. Without friction, the passenger's feet would remain in their initial position relative to the ground, and the bus floor would slide forward beneath them.

Question 24hard

Which of the following statements accurately represents Newton's Second Law of Motion?

  1. Every action has an equal and opposite reaction.
  2. An object at rest stays at rest, and an object in motion stays in motion with the same speed and in the same direction unless acted upon by an unbalanced force.
  3. The rate of change of momentum of a body is directly proportional to the applied force and takes place in the direction in which the force acts.
  4. Force is equal to mass times acceleration (F = ma).
Show answer

Answer: The rate of change of momentum of a body is directly proportional to the applied force and takes place in the direction in which the force acts.

Newton's Second Law of Motion, in its most fundamental form, states that the net external force acting on an object is directly proportional to the rate of change of its momentum, and this change in momentum occurs in the direction of the applied force. While F=ma is a common derived form for constant mass, the definition involving momentum is more general. Option 0 is Newton's Third Law, and Option 1 is Newton's First Law.

Question 25hard

Which of the following statements accurately describes forces according to Newton's Third Law?

  1. Forces always occur singly in nature.
  2. Mutual forces between two interacting bodies are always equal in magnitude and in the same direction.
  3. Forces always occur in pairs, and the mutual forces between two interacting bodies are equal in magnitude and opposite in direction.
  4. Forces can occur singly or in pairs, depending on the situation.
Show answer

Answer: Forces always occur in pairs, and the mutual forces between two interacting bodies are equal in magnitude and opposite in direction.

Newton's Third Law states that for every action, there is an equal and opposite reaction. This means forces never occur singly; they always come in pairs. These mutual forces are always equal in magnitude but act in opposite directions on the two interacting bodies.

Question 26hard

What is the fundamental principle of the law of conservation of momentum?

  1. The total momentum of a system always increases over time.
  2. The total momentum of an isolated system of interacting particles remains constant.
  3. Momentum is conserved only if external forces are acting on the system.
  4. The momentum of individual particles within a system is always conserved.
Show answer

Answer: The total momentum of an isolated system of interacting particles remains constant.

The law of conservation of momentum states that for an isolated system (one where no external forces act), the total momentum of the system remains constant over time, regardless of interactions between particles within the system.

Question 27hard

A body of mass 'm' is at rest on a horizontal table. If a small horizontal force 'F' is applied, and the body remains at rest, which of the following best explains this observation?

  1. Newton's second law (F=ma) is contradicted in this scenario.
  2. The applied force 'F' is not strong enough to overcome the body's inertia.
  3. There is an opposing horizontal force, such as static friction, that balances the applied force 'F', resulting in zero net force.
  4. The mass 'm' of the body is too large for the applied force 'F' to cause any acceleration.
Show answer

Answer: There is an opposing horizontal force, such as static friction, that balances the applied force 'F', resulting in zero net force.

If a body remains at rest despite an applied force, it means the net force acting on it is zero. This is consistent with Newton's second law (F_net = ma, where a=0). The opposing force is typically static friction, which adjusts its magnitude to match the applied force up to a certain limit, thus keeping the body at rest.

Question 28hard

Which of the following is the primary reason for the occurrence of rolling friction?

  1. The continuous sliding of one surface over another.
  2. The strong adhesive forces between the rolling body and the surface.
  3. The momentary deformation of the surfaces in contact, leading to energy dissipation.
  4. The air resistance acting on the rolling body.
Show answer

Answer: The momentary deformation of the surfaces in contact, leading to energy dissipation.

Rolling friction arises from the complex process of continuous deformation and recovery of the surfaces in contact. As the rolling body moves, the surfaces deform slightly, creating a finite contact area. This deformation and subsequent recovery dissipate energy, which is manifested as rolling friction.

Question 29hard

What is the significance of the 'optimum speed' (v_o = (R g tan θ)^(1/2)) for a vehicle on a banked road?

  1. At this speed, the vehicle experiences the maximum possible frictional force.
  2. It is the speed at which the vehicle is most likely to skid off the road.
  3. At this speed, the horizontal component of the normal reaction provides the entire centripetal force, eliminating the need for friction.
  4. It is the minimum speed required to safely navigate the banked curve.
Show answer

Answer: At this speed, the horizontal component of the normal reaction provides the entire centripetal force, eliminating the need for friction.

The optimum speed on a banked road is the specific speed at which the horizontal component of the normal reaction force is exactly sufficient to provide the necessary centripetal force. This means that no frictional force is required to keep the vehicle on the curve, leading to minimal wear and tear on the tyres and a safer ride.

Question 30hard

Why are free-body diagrams considered essential tools in solving mechanics problems?

  1. They help in calculating the internal forces within a system.
  2. They simplify the problem by ignoring all forces acting on the system.
  3. They clearly define the system and identify all external forces acting on it.
  4. They are primarily used for visualizing the motion of the system, not for force analysis.
Show answer

Answer: They clearly define the system and identify all external forces acting on it.

Free-body diagrams are crucial because they isolate the system of interest and graphically represent all external forces acting *on* that system. This clear visualization helps in applying Newton's laws correctly by ensuring all relevant forces are accounted for and internal forces are excluded from the analysis of the system's motion.

Question 31hard

In mechanics, terms like 'friction', 'normal reaction', 'tension', and 'weight' fundamentally represent what, and how should they be generally expressed for clarity?

  1. They represent different types of energy, and should be expressed as 'energy of A by B'.
  2. They are all types of forces, and should be reduced to the phrase 'force on A by B'.
  3. They represent different forms of momentum, and should be expressed as 'momentum of A by B'.
  4. They are all scalar quantities, and their direction is not important.
Show answer

Answer: They are all types of forces, and should be reduced to the phrase 'force on A by B'.

All these terms ('friction', 'normal reaction', 'tension', 'weight', 'centripetal force') are specific manifestations or contexts of the fundamental concept of 'force'. For clarity and consistency in mechanics, any force should be precisely described using the format 'force on A by B', indicating the object experiencing the force (A) and the object exerting the force (B).

Question 32hard

A batsman deflects a ball of mass 0.15 kg by an angle of 45° without changing its initial speed of 54 km/h. What is the magnitude of the impulse imparted to the ball? (Given: √2 ≈ 1.414)

  1. 0.76 Ns
  2. 1.15 Ns
  3. 1.72 Ns
  4. 2.25 Ns
Show answer

Answer: 1.72 Ns

Mass of the ball, m = 0.15 kg. Initial speed, u = 54 km/h = 54 * (1000/3600) m/s = 15 m/s. Final speed, v = 15 m/s (speed remains unchanged). Angle of deflection, θ = 45°. Impulse imparted, J = Change in momentum, Δp = m(v⃗ - u⃗). The magnitude of the change in velocity, |Δv⃗| = |v⃗ - u⃗|, can be found using the law of cosines: |Δv⃗|² = |v⃗|² + |u⃗|² - 2|v⃗||u⃗|cos(θ) |Δv⃗|² = 15² + 15² - 2(15)(15)cos(45°) |Δv⃗|² = 2 * 15² - 2 * 15² * (1/√2) |Δv⃗|² = 2 * 15² * (1 - 1/√2) |Δv⃗| = 15 * √(2 * (1 - 1/√2)) = 15 * √(2 - √2) |Δv⃗| = 15 * √(2 - 1.414) = 15 * √(0.586) ≈ 15 * 0.7655 ≈ 11.4825 m/s. Magnitude of impulse, |J| = m * |Δv⃗| = 0.15 kg * 11.4825 m/s ≈ 1.722 Ns.

Question 33hard

When two vectors are subjected to a scalar product (dot product) operation, the resulting quantity is:

  1. Always a vector quantity
  2. Always a scalar quantity
  3. Sometimes a scalar, sometimes a vector, depending on the vectors
  4. A dimensionless quantity
Show answer

Answer: Always a scalar quantity

The scalar product, also known as the dot product, of two vectors yields a scalar quantity. This means the result has only magnitude and no direction. For example, work done (W = F ⋅ d) is a scalar quantity.

Question 34hard

In the context of work done by a variable force F(x) over a small displacement Δx, how is the work done (ΔW) best approximated?

  1. ΔW = F(x) / Δx
  2. ΔW = F(x) + Δx
  3. ΔW = F(x) ⋅ Δx
  4. ΔW = F(x) - Δx
Show answer

Answer: ΔW = F(x) ⋅ Δx

When the displacement Δx is very small, the variable force F(x) can be considered approximately constant over that interval. Therefore, the work done (ΔW) is approximated as the product of the force and the displacement, i.e., ΔW = F(x) ⋅ Δx. This forms the basis for calculating work done by integration for larger displacements.

Question 35hard

In the relation F = -dV(h)/dh for gravitational force, what does the negative sign primarily signify?

  1. The force is always attractive.
  2. The force is directed upwards, opposite to the potential energy gradient.
  3. The force is directed downwards, opposite to the conventional positive direction for height 'h'.
  4. The potential energy is decreasing with increasing height.
Show answer

Answer: The force is directed downwards, opposite to the conventional positive direction for height 'h'.

The negative sign in F = -dV(h)/dh indicates that the gravitational force acts in a direction opposite to the increase in potential energy. If 'h' is taken as positive upwards, then an increase in 'h' leads to an increase in potential energy, but the gravitational force acts downwards. Hence, the negative sign signifies that the gravitational force is directed downwards, opposite to the upward positive direction for height 'h'.

Question 36hard

A bob undergoing vertical circular motion has its string slacken at the highest point C. If the string is cut at this exact instant, what will be the subsequent motion of the bob?

  1. It will fall straight down vertically.
  2. It will continue in a circular path due to inertia.
  3. It will execute projectile motion with a horizontal projection.
  4. It will move upwards for some time before falling down.
Show answer

Answer: It will execute projectile motion with a horizontal projection.

When the string slackens at the highest point C, the tension (T_C) becomes zero. At this moment, the gravitational force provides the necessary centripetal force (mg = mv_C²/L). If the string is cut, the bob will have a horizontal velocity (v_C) and will be under the influence of gravity. This scenario is identical to an object being kicked horizontally from a cliff, resulting in projectile motion with a horizontal projection.

Question 37hard

Which of the following pairs correctly differentiates between a conservative and a non-conservative force, along with an appropriate example for each?

  1. Conservative: Friction (conserves mechanical energy); Non-conservative: Spring force (does not conserve mechanical energy)
  2. Conservative: Gravitational force (conserves mechanical energy); Non-conservative: Air resistance (does not conserve mechanical energy)
  3. Conservative: Applied force (conserves mechanical energy); Non-conservative: Magnetic force (does not conserve mechanical energy)
  4. Conservative: Normal force (conserves mechanical energy); Non-conservative: Elastic force (does not conserve mechanical energy)
Show answer

Answer: Conservative: Gravitational force (conserves mechanical energy); Non-conservative: Air resistance (does not conserve mechanical energy)

Conservative forces, such as gravitational force and spring force, allow for the conservation of mechanical energy (potential + kinetic). The work done by a conservative force depends only on the initial and final positions, not on the path taken. Non-conservative forces, such as friction and air resistance, dissipate mechanical energy, converting it into other forms like heat. The work done by a non-conservative force depends on the path taken.

Question 38hard

Which of the following statements accurately defines an elastic collision based on energy conservation?

  1. An elastic collision is one where only the total linear momentum is conserved.
  2. An elastic collision is one where the total kinetic energy is conserved, but not necessarily the total linear momentum.
  3. An elastic collision is one where both the total linear momentum and the total kinetic energy of the system are conserved.
  4. An elastic collision is one where some kinetic energy is lost due to deformation, but momentum is conserved.
Show answer

Answer: An elastic collision is one where both the total linear momentum and the total kinetic energy of the system are conserved.

An elastic collision is characterized by the conservation of both total linear momentum and total kinetic energy of the system. This implies that there is no net loss of kinetic energy during the collision, meaning any deformation that occurs is fully recovered.

Question 39hard

How does a 'scattering' event in physics differ from an everyday 'collision'?

  1. A 'collision' involves forces acting at a distance, while 'scattering' involves physical contact.
  2. A 'scattering' event always results in the objects sticking together, unlike a 'collision'.
  3. A 'collision' typically involves physical contact between bodies, whereas 'scattering' involves forces acting at a distance without necessarily touching.
  4. Both 'collision' and 'scattering' are identical terms used interchangeably in physics.
Show answer

Answer: A 'collision' typically involves physical contact between bodies, whereas 'scattering' involves forces acting at a distance without necessarily touching.

An everyday 'collision' typically implies physical contact between two bodies, like in billiards or carrom. In contrast, a 'scattering' event in physics involves interactions where forces act at a distance, and the bodies do not necessarily touch. Examples include a comet interacting with the Sun's gravity or an alpha particle being deflected by a nucleus.

Question 40hard

For a particle moving under a potential energy function V(x) with total energy E, why can the particle not be found in regions where E < V(x)?

  1. Because the potential energy would be negative, which is impossible.
  2. Because the total energy would be negative, which is impossible.
  3. Because the kinetic energy (K = E - V(x)) would be negative, which is physically impossible.
  4. Because the force acting on the particle would be zero in such regions.
Show answer

Answer: Because the kinetic energy (K = E - V(x)) would be negative, which is physically impossible.

The total mechanical energy (E) of a particle is the sum of its kinetic energy (K) and potential energy (V), so E = K + V. Therefore, K = E - V. If E < V(x), then E - V(x) would be a negative value. Since kinetic energy (K = 1/2 mv²) must always be non-negative (as mass 'm' and velocity squared 'v²' are always positive or zero), a negative kinetic energy is physically impossible. Hence, the particle cannot exist in such regions.

Question 41hard

The mass of air (m) passing through a circular area A in time t, when the wind flows at a velocity v perpendicular to the circle, is given by the formula:

  1. m = ρ × (A × v)
  2. m = ρ × (A × t)
  3. m = ρ × (A × v × t)
  4. m = ρ × (v × t)
Show answer

Answer: m = ρ × (A × v × t)

The mass of air (m) is the product of its density (ρ) and the volume of air passing through. The volume of air passing through the area A in time t is given by the product of the area and the distance covered by the wind, which is v × t. Therefore, the volume is A × v × t. So, m = ρ × (A × v × t).

A rigid body can be constrained to have only rotational motion by fixing it along a straight line. This fixed line then acts as its axis of rotation, preventing any translational movement of the body as a whole.

Question 44hard

The center of mass of a system of particles depends on both the positions and the masses of the particles. Question 45hard

Why do the internal forces generated during an explosion of a projectile not alter the trajectory of its center of mass?

  1. Internal forces are always balanced.
  2. The explosion occurs instantaneously.
  3. Only external forces can change the motion of the center of mass.
  4. The projectile's mass changes during the explosion.
Show answer

Answer: Only external forces can change the motion of the center of mass.

According to Newton's second law for a system of particles, the acceleration of the center of mass is determined solely by the net external force acting on the system. Internal forces, by definition, act between particles within the system and cancel out in pairs (Newton's third law), thus having no net effect on the motion of the center of mass. Therefore, the trajectory of the center of mass remains unchanged by internal forces like those from an explosion.

Question 47hard

  4. The center of mass remains stationary.

Pure rotation of a rigid body is characterized by all its constituent particles or parts having the same angular velocity at any given instant of time. In contrast, pure translation is characterized by all parts having the same linear velocity.

Question 48hard

What are the dimensions of the moment of force (torque)?

  1. M L T⁻¹
  2. M L² T⁻²
  3. M L T⁻²
  4. M L⁻¹ T⁻²
Show answer

Answer: M L² T⁻²

Moment of force (torque, τ) is defined as the product of force (F) and the perpendicular distance (r) from the axis of rotation to the line of action of the force (τ = r × F). The dimensions of force are [M L T⁻²] and the dimensions of distance are [L]. Therefore, the dimensions of torque are [L] × [M L T⁻²] = [M L² T⁻²].

Question 49hard

Under which conditions does the contribution of internal forces to the total torque on a system of particles become zero?

  1. Only if Newton's third law of motion holds.
  2. Only if internal forces are directed along the line joining the particles.
  3. If Newton's third law of motion holds AND internal forces are directed along the line joining the particles.
  4. If the system is in translational equilibrium.
Show answer

Answer: If Newton's third law of motion holds AND internal forces are directed along the line joining the particles.

The contribution of internal forces to the total torque on a system of particles becomes zero when two conditions are met: 1) Newton's third law of motion applies, ensuring that forces between any two particles are equal and opposite, and 2) these internal forces are directed along the line connecting the two particles. This alignment causes the torque generated by each action-reaction pair of internal forces to cancel out.

Question 50hard

  2. The sum of forces along any two perpendicular axes is zero, and the sum of torques about any axis perpendicular to the plane is zero.
  3. The sum of forces along any two perpendicular axes is zero, and the sum of torques about any point in the plane is zero.
  4. The sum of forces along one axis is zero, and the sum of torques about any axis perpendicular to the plane is zero.
Show answer

Answer: The sum of forces along any two perpendicular axes is zero, and the sum of torques about any axis perpendicular to the plane is zero.

For coplanar forces, mechanical equilibrium requires two conditions for translational equilibrium (sum of force components along any two perpendicular axes in the plane must be zero) and one condition for rotational equilibrium (sum of torque components along any axis perpendicular to the plane of forces must be zero).

Question 52hard

What is the kinetic energy of a rigid body rotating about a fixed axis with angular velocity ω and moment of inertia I?

  1. K = Iω
  2. K = (1/2)Iω
  3. K = (1/2)Iω^2
  4. K = Iω^2
Show answer

Answer: K = (1/2)Iω^2

For a particle of mass m_i at distance r_i from the axis, its linear velocity is v_i = r_iω. Its kinetic energy is k_i = (1/2)m_i v_i^2 = (1/2)m_i (r_iω)^2. The total kinetic energy (K) of the body is the sum of individual particle kinetic energies: K = Σ k_i = Σ (1/2)m_i r_i^2 ω^2. Since ω is the same for all particles, K = (1/2) (Σ m_i r_i^2) ω^2. Substituting the definition of moment of inertia I = Σ m_i r_i^2, we get K = (1/2)Iω^2.

  3. (1/5)MR²
  4. (2/3)MR²
Show answer

Answer: (2/5)MR²

According to standard formulas for moments of inertia, the moment of inertia of a solid sphere of radius R and mass M about its diameter is (2/5)MR².

Question 54hard

When multiple forces act on a rigid body rotating about a fixed axis, how is the total work done (dW) calculated?

  1. dW = (τ1 - τ2 - ...)dθ
  2. dW = (τ1 + τ2 + ...)dθ
  3. dW = (τ1 × τ2 × ...)dθ
  4. dW = (τ1 / τ2 / ...)dθ
Show answer

Answer: dW = (τ1 + τ2 + ...)dθ

When multiple forces act on a body rotating about a fixed axis, the total work done (dW) is the algebraic sum of the work done by each force. Since all torques considered are parallel to the fixed axis and the angular displacement dθ is the same for all particles, the total work done is given by dW = (τ1 + τ2 + ...)dθ, where τ is the magnitude of the total (external) torque.

Question 56hard

How does a ballet dancer performing a pirouette increase their angular speed?

  1. By increasing their moment of inertia by stretching their arms.
  2. By decreasing their moment of inertia by bringing their arms closer to their body.
  3. By applying an external torque to their body.
  4. By increasing their mass during the pirouette.
Show answer

Answer: By decreasing their moment of inertia by bringing their arms closer to their body.

A ballet dancer performing a pirouette utilizes the conservation of angular momentum. When the dancer brings their arms closer to their body, their moment of inertia (I) about the axis of rotation decreases. Since the external torque is negligible, the total angular momentum (L = Iω) remains constant. Consequently, to conserve angular momentum, their angular speed (ω) increases.

According to the principle of conservation of angular momentum, L = Iω = constant. If the moment of inertia (I) decreases, the angular speed (ω) must increase proportionally to maintain the constancy of angular momentum.

Question 60hard

For small heights 'h' (where h << RE), which of the following is the approximate formula for the acceleration due to gravity, g(h)?

  1. g(h) ≈ g(1 + h/RE)
  2. g(h) ≈ g(1 - h/RE)
  3. g(h) ≈ g(1 - 2h/RE)
  4. g(h) ≈ g(1 + 2h/RE)
Show answer

Answer: g(h) ≈ g(1 - 2h/RE)

The acceleration due to gravity at height h is given by g(h) = GM/(RE+h)^2. For h << RE, we can use the binomial approximation (1+x)^n ≈ 1+nx. So, g(h) = GM/[RE^2(1+h/RE)^2] = g(1+h/RE)^-2 ≈ g(1 - 2h/RE).

Question 61hard

  4. By finding the potential energy of the center of mass; Newton's Second Law.
Show answer

Answer: By summing the potential energies of all possible distinct pairs; Superposition Principle.

The total gravitational potential energy of a system of multiple particles is determined by summing the gravitational potential energies for all possible distinct pairs of its constituent particles. This is a direct application of the superposition principle, which states that the total potential energy is the algebraic sum of the potential energies due to individual pairs.

Question 64hard

For an orbiting satellite, if the zero of potential energy is taken at infinity, what is the relationship between its total mechanical energy (E), kinetic energy (K), and potential energy (U) in a stable circular orbit?

  1. E = K + U, and E = K
  2. E = K + U, and E = U
  3. E = K + U, and E = -K
  4. E = K + U, and E = 2K
Show answer

Answer: E = K + U, and E = -K

For a stable circular orbit, the kinetic energy (K) is equal to half the magnitude of the potential energy (U), i.e., K = -U/2. Therefore, the total mechanical energy E = K + U = K + (-2K) = -K. Alternatively, E = U/2. The total energy is negative of its kinetic energy.

Question 65hard

  2. The digit '6' is uncertain, and it has 2 significant figures.
  3. The digit '2' is uncertain, and it has 3 significant figures.
  4. All digits are certain, and it has 3 significant figures.
Show answer

Answer: The digit '2' is uncertain, and it has 3 significant figures.

In any measurement, the last reported digit is considered uncertain. Here, '1' and '6' are reliable, while '2' is the first uncertain digit. The number of significant figures includes all reliable digits plus the first uncertain digit, making it 3 significant figures (1, 6, and 2).

Question 66hard

When performing arithmetic operations with approximate measured values, what is the primary rule for maintaining accuracy regarding significant figures?

  1. The result should always have more significant figures than any of the original values to show improved precision.
  2. The result should be rounded to the nearest whole number, regardless of the significant figures in the original data.
  3. The result must reflect the uncertainties in the original measured values and cannot be more accurate than the original data with the least number of significant figures.
  4. The result should have the same number of significant figures as the original value with the most significant figures.
Show answer

Answer: The result must reflect the uncertainties in the original measured values and cannot be more accurate than the original data with the least number of significant figures.

The fundamental principle is that the accuracy of a calculated result cannot exceed the accuracy of the least precise measurement used in the calculation. Therefore, the final result must be limited by the original data having the fewest significant figures.

Question 69hard

One mole of an ideal gas at STP occupies 22.4 L. If the atomic volume of a mole of hydrogen is approximately 3.156 × 10⁻⁷ m³, what is the approximate ratio of molar volume to atomic volume, and why is this ratio so large?

  1. Ratio ≈ 7.1 × 10², because gas molecules are very small.
  2. Ratio ≈ 7.1 × 10⁴, because gas molecules are widely separated with much empty space.
  3. Ratio ≈ 7.1 × 10⁻⁴, because atomic volume is much larger than molar volume.
  4. Ratio ≈ 7.1 × 10⁶, because gas molecules are tightly packed.
Show answer

Answer: Ratio ≈ 7.1 × 10⁴, because gas molecules are widely separated with much empty space.

Molar volume = 22.4 L = 22.4 × 10⁻³ m³. Atomic volume ≈ 3.156 × 10⁻⁷ m³. Ratio = (22.4 × 10⁻³ m³) / (3.156 × 10⁻⁷ m³) ≈ 7.098 × 10⁴. This large ratio indicates that in a gas, the actual volume occupied by the molecules themselves is a tiny fraction of the total volume, with the vast majority being empty space between the widely separated molecules.

Question 70hard

  1. By finding the integral of the position function with respect to time (v = ∫x dt).
  2. By finding the derivative of the position function with respect to time (v = dx/dt).
  3. By dividing the total displacement by the total time taken (v = Δx/Δt).
  4. By multiplying the position function by time (v = x * t).
Show answer

Answer: By finding the derivative of the position function with respect to time (v = dx/dt).

Instantaneous velocity is defined as the rate of change of position with respect to time. In calculus, this is precisely what the first derivative of the position function (x) with respect to time (t) represents, i.e., v = dx/dt.

Question 71hard

In realistic physical situations, why are graphs of position, velocity, and acceleration always smooth without sharp kinks?

  1. Because instruments used for measurement always smooth out the data.
  2. Because changes in physical quantities are always continuous, implying that the functions are differentiable at all points.
  3. Because sharp kinks would violate the laws of conservation of energy.
  4. Because it is easier to draw smooth graphs in textbooks.
Show answer

Answer: Because changes in physical quantities are always continuous, implying that the functions are differentiable at all points.

Physical processes in the real world are continuous. An instantaneous, abrupt change in velocity (a sharp kink in a velocity-time graph) would imply infinite acceleration, which is physically impossible. Similarly, an abrupt change in position would imply infinite velocity. Therefore, the functions representing these quantities must be differentiable, leading to smooth graphs.

Question 72hard

For a body falling from rest, Galileo's law of odd numbers states that the distances traversed in successive equal time intervals are in the ratio of:

  1. 1:2:3
  2. 1:3:5
  3. 1:4:9
  4. 1:1:1
Show answer

Answer: 1:3:5

For a body falling from rest, the distance fallen is y = ½gt². If we consider equal time intervals (e.g., τ, 2τ, 3τ...), the positions will be ½gτ², ½g(2τ)² = 4(½gτ²), ½g(3τ)² = 9(½gτ²), and so on. The distances traversed in successive equal time intervals are then: 1st interval: ½gτ²; 2nd interval: 4(½gτ²) - ½gτ² = 3(½gτ²); 3rd interval: 9(½gτ²) - 4(½gτ²) = 5(½gτ²). The ratio of these distances is 1:3:5, confirming Galileo's law.

Two vectors A and B are said to be equal if, and only if, they fulfill two conditions: they must have the same magnitude AND they must have the same direction. Both conditions are essential and sufficient.

When two velocity vectors, such as the vertical velocity of rain (v_r) and the horizontal velocity of wind (v_w), are perpendicular, the magnitude of their resultant velocity (R) is calculated using the Pythagorean theorem: R = sqrt(v_r^2 + v_w^2).

Question 78hard

In the derivation of the magnitude of centripetal acceleration in uniform circular motion, which similarity property between two triangles is crucial?

  1. Similarity between the triangle formed by position vectors and the triangle formed by acceleration vectors.
  2. Similarity between the triangle formed by position vectors and the triangle formed by velocity vectors.
  3. Similarity between the triangle formed by velocity vectors and the triangle formed by force vectors.
  4. Similarity between the triangle formed by displacement vectors and the triangle formed by momentum vectors.
Show answer

Answer: Similarity between the triangle formed by position vectors and the triangle formed by velocity vectors.

The derivation of centripetal acceleration relies on the similarity between the triangle formed by the position vectors (r, r', and Δr) and the triangle formed by the velocity vectors (v, v', and Δv). This similarity arises because the velocity vector is always perpendicular to the position vector, ensuring that the angle between r and r' is equal to the angle between v and v'. This allows us to equate ratios of corresponding sides, leading to the expression for centripetal acceleration.

Question 79hard

Which of the following correctly defines the instantaneous velocity of an object at time 't'?

  1. The average velocity over a very large time interval.
  2. The limiting value of its average velocity as the time interval Δt approaches infinity.
  3. The limiting value of its average velocity as the time interval Δt tends to zero.
  4. The total displacement divided by the total time taken.
Show answer

Answer: The limiting value of its average velocity as the time interval Δt tends to zero.

Instantaneous velocity is defined as the limiting value of the average velocity as the time interval Δt approaches zero. Mathematically, it is expressed as v = lim (Δt→0) (Δr / Δt) = dr / dt. This represents the velocity of the object at a specific instant in time.

Question 80hard

Consider the statement: 'Three vectors not lying in a plane can never add up to give a null vector.' Is this statement true or false, and why?

  1. False, because any three vectors can always form a closed triangle, resulting in a null vector.
  2. True, because for their sum to be null, the resultant of two vectors must be collinear with the third, which is impossible if they are non-coplanar.
  3. False, because vector addition is commutative and associative, allowing for a null sum regardless of coplanarity.
  4. True, because a null vector can only be formed by vectors acting along the same line.
Show answer

Answer: True, because for their sum to be null, the resultant of two vectors must be collinear with the third, which is impossible if they are non-coplanar.

The statement is true. For three vectors A, B, and C to sum to a null vector (A + B + C = 0), the resultant of any two (e.g., A + B) must be equal in magnitude and opposite in direction to the third vector (-C). The resultant (A + B) will always lie in the plane formed by A and B. For -C to be collinear with (A + B), C must also lie in the same plane. Therefore, if the three vectors are not coplanar, their sum cannot be a null vector.

The preceding chapter in NCERT Physics (likely 'Motion in a Straight Line' and 'Motion in a Plane') primarily focused on kinematics, which involves quantitatively describing the motion of a particle in space without considering the causes of motion (forces).

Question 82hard

What new insight did Galileo provide regarding the states of rest and uniform linear motion?

  1. He proved that the state of rest is fundamentally different from uniform linear motion.
  2. He concluded that uniform linear motion requires a constant net force.
  3. He established that the state of rest and uniform linear motion are equivalent, both implying no net force.
  4. He demonstrated that only the state of rest implies zero net force.
Show answer

Answer: He established that the state of rest and uniform linear motion are equivalent, both implying no net force.

Galileo's crucial insight was that the state of rest and the state of uniform linear motion (motion with constant velocity) are equivalent. In both scenarios, there is no net external force acting on the body. This concept laid the foundation for Newton's First Law of Motion (Law of Inertia).

Question 83hard

  4. Friction helps the passenger maintain their balance by increasing their effective weight.
Show answer

Answer: Friction between the passenger's feet and the bus floor provides the forward accelerating force.

During a moderate start, the static friction between the passenger's feet and the bus floor provides the external force required to accelerate the passenger along with the bus. Without this frictional force, the passenger's feet would slip backward relative to the bus floor due to inertia, and the passenger would tend to remain in their initial state of rest or uniform motion.

Question 84hard

According to Newton's Third Law, what are the key characteristics of forces as they occur in nature?

  2. Forces always occur in pairs, and the mutual forces between two interacting bodies are equal in magnitude and opposite in direction.

Show answer

Answer: Forces always occur in pairs, and the mutual forces between two interacting bodies are equal in magnitude and opposite in direction.

Newton's Third Law of Motion states that forces never occur singly; they always occur in pairs. Furthermore, for every action, there is an equal and opposite reaction. This means that the mutual forces between two interacting bodies are always equal in magnitude and opposite in direction.

The law of conservation of momentum states that for an isolated system (where no external forces act), the total momentum of the system remains constant. This means the initial total momentum equals the final total momentum.

Question 90hard

In mechanics, terms like 'friction', 'normal reaction', 'tension', and 'weight' fundamentally represent what, and how should they be expressed for clarity?

  1. They represent different types of energy and should be expressed as 'energy of A by B'.
  2. They are all fundamentally 'forces' and should be expressed as 'force on A by B'.
  3. They are all types of acceleration and should be expressed as 'acceleration of A by B'.
  4. They represent different forms of momentum and should be expressed as 'momentum of A by B'.
Show answer

Answer: They are all fundamentally 'forces' and should be expressed as 'force on A by B'.

All these terms ('friction', 'normal reaction', 'tension', 'weight', 'centripetal force') are specific manifestations or contexts of 'force'. For clarity and proper analysis in mechanics, any force should be explicitly stated as 'force on A by B', indicating the object experiencing the force (A) and the object exerting the force (B).

Question 91hard

A batsman deflects a cricket ball (mass = 0.15 kg) by an angle of 45° without changing its initial speed of 54 km/h. What is the magnitude of the impulse imparted to the ball? (Given: √2 ≈ 1.414)

  1. 1.72 Ns
  2. 2.25 Ns
  3. 0.75 Ns
  4. 3.00 Ns
Show answer

Answer: 1.72 Ns

Given: Mass m = 0.15 kg. Initial speed u = 54 km/h = 15 m/s. Final speed v = 15 m/s. Angle of deflection θ = 45°. Impulse J = Change in momentum Δp = m(v - u). The magnitude of the change in velocity |Δv| can be found using the law of cosines: |Δv|² = v² + u² - 2vu cos(θ) |Δv|² = 15² + 15² - 2(15)(15)cos(45°) |Δv|² = 2 * 15² - 2 * 15² * (1/√2) |Δv|² = 2 * 15² * (1 - 1/√2) |Δv| = 15 * √(2 * (1 - 1/√2)) = 15 * √(2 - √2) |Δv| = 15 * √(2 - 1.414) = 15 * √(0.586) ≈ 15 * 0.7655 ≈ 11.4825 m/s. Magnitude of impulse |J| = m * |Δv| = 0.15 kg * 11.4825 m/s ≈ 1.722 Ns. Rounding to two decimal places, the impulse is approximately 1.72 Ns.

Question 93hard

Question 95hard

Question 96hard

Which of the following statements correctly differentiates between conservative and non-conservative forces?

  1. Conservative forces always increase mechanical energy, while non-conservative forces always decrease it.

Show answer

Answer: Conservative forces (e.g., spring force) conserve mechanical energy, while non-conservative forces (e.g., friction) do not.

Conservative forces, such as gravitational force and spring force, are path-independent and allow for the conservation of mechanical energy (potential + kinetic). Non-conservative forces, like friction and air resistance, are path-dependent and dissipate mechanical energy, converting it into other forms like heat.

Question 99hard

Why is a particle with total energy E unable to be found in regions where its potential energy V(x) is greater than E?

  1. Because the force acting on the particle would be zero.
  2. Because its kinetic energy would be negative, which is physically impossible.
  3. Because the particle would be at rest in such regions.
  4. Because the potential energy function is undefined there.
Show answer

Answer: Because its kinetic energy would be negative, which is physically impossible.

The total energy E of a particle is the sum of its kinetic energy (K) and potential energy (V), so E = K + V. If E < V(x), then K = E - V(x) would be negative. Kinetic energy, being proportional to the square of velocity (1/2 mv²), cannot be negative. Therefore, the particle cannot exist in regions where its potential energy exceeds its total energy.

Question 100hard

If wind flows at a velocity 'v' perpendicular to a circular area 'A' for a time 't', and the air density is 'ρ', what is the correct formula for the mass of air (m) passing through the area?

  1. m = ρ * A * v / t
  2. m = ρ * A * v * t
  3. m = ρ * A / (v * t)
  4. m = A * v * t / ρ
Show answer

Answer: m = ρ * A * v * t

The volume of air passing through the area A in time t is given by the product of the area and the distance covered by the wind, which is v * t. So, Volume = A * v * t. Since mass = density * volume, the mass of air is m = ρ * (A * v * t).

Question 101hard

To achieve pure rotational motion, all translational movement must be prevented. Fixing the rigid body along a straight line effectively creates a fixed axis of rotation, allowing only rotation about that axis.

Question 105hard

  4. The center of mass of the body remains stationary.

Pure rotation is characterized by every particle in the rigid body having the same angular velocity at any given instant. In contrast, pure translation means all parts have the same linear velocity.

Question 106hard

Under what conditions does the contribution of internal forces to the total torque on a system of particles become zero?

  1. Only if the system is in translational equilibrium.
  2. If Newton's third law holds and internal forces are perpendicular to the line joining particles.
  3. If Newton's third law holds and internal forces are directed along the line joining the particles.
  4. Only if the system is isolated from external forces.
Show answer

Answer: If Newton's third law holds and internal forces are directed along the line joining the particles.

The contribution of internal forces to the total torque is zero if two conditions are met: 1) Newton's third law applies (action-reaction pairs are equal and opposite), and 2) these internal forces act along the line joining the two particles. This ensures that the torque produced by each action-reaction pair cancels out.

Question 107hard

For a rigid body under coplanar forces, which set of conditions ensures mechanical equilibrium?

  1. Sum of forces in one direction is zero, and sum of torques about one point is zero.
  2. Sum of forces in any two perpendicular directions is zero, and sum of torques about any axis perpendicular to the plane is zero.
  3. Sum of forces in any direction is zero, and sum of torques about any point is zero.
  4. Sum of forces in one direction is zero, and sum of torques about the center of mass is zero.
Show answer

Answer: Sum of forces in any two perpendicular directions is zero, and sum of torques about any axis perpendicular to the plane is zero.

For mechanical equilibrium under coplanar forces, both translational and rotational equilibrium must be satisfied. Translational equilibrium requires the net force to be zero, which means the sum of force components along any two perpendicular axes must be zero. Rotational equilibrium requires the net torque to be zero, meaning the sum of torques about any axis perpendicular to the plane of forces must be zero.

Question 108hard

According to a balancing experiment, how is the Centre of Gravity (CG) of a body defined?

  1. The point where the body's mass is concentrated.
  2. The point where the body can be balanced on a support, remaining horizontal.
  3. The geometric center of the body.
  4. The point where external forces are applied to cause rotation.
Show answer

Answer: The point where the body can be balanced on a support, remaining horizontal.

The Centre of Gravity (CG) is defined as the point where the entire weight of the body appears to act. In a balancing experiment, it's the point where the body can be supported (e.g., on the tip of a finger) and remain in stable mechanical equilibrium, i.e., horizontal, without toppling.

Question 109hard

Which of the following expressions correctly represents the kinetic energy of a rigid body rotating about a fixed axis?

  1. K = (1/2)mv^2
  2. K = (1/2)Iω^2
  3. K = Iα
  4. K = (1/2)mω^2
Show answer

Answer: K = (1/2)Iω^2

The kinetic energy of a rigid body rotating about a fixed axis is analogous to translational kinetic energy. For a particle, K = (1/2)mv^2. For rotational motion, mass (m) is replaced by moment of inertia (I) and linear velocity (v) is replaced by angular velocity (ω). Thus, K = (1/2)Iω^2. This is derived by summing the kinetic energies of individual particles (k_i = (1/2)m_i r_i^2 ω^2) and factoring out (1/2)ω^2, leaving Σm_i r_i^2, which is the definition of moment of inertia (I).

Question 110hard

According to standard formulas for moments of inertia, what is the moment of inertia of a solid sphere of mass M and radius R about its diameter?

  1. (1/2)MR^2
  2. (2/5)MR^2
  3. (1/3)MR^2
  4. MR^2
Show answer

Answer: (2/5)MR^2

The moment of inertia of a solid sphere of mass M and radius R about an axis passing through its diameter is a standard result in rotational dynamics, given by the formula (2/5)MR^2. This value is typically provided in tables of moments of inertia for various standard shapes.

Question 111hard

When multiple forces act on a rigid body rotating about a fixed axis, how is the total work done (dW) calculated for an infinitesimal angular displacement (dθ)?

  1. dW = (τ1 - τ2 - ...)dθ
  2. dW = (τ1 + τ2 + ...)dθ
  3. dW = (τ1 × τ2 × ...)dθ
  4. dW = (τ1 / τ2 / ...)dθ
Show answer

Answer: dW = (τ1 + τ2 + ...)dθ

For a rigid body rotating about a fixed axis, the work done by a torque is given by τdθ. When multiple forces act, they produce individual torques (τ1, τ2, etc.). Since the angular displacement (dθ) is the same for all particles and torques are considered parallel to the fixed axis, the total work done is the algebraic sum of the work done by each torque. Therefore, dW = (τ1 + τ2 + ...)dθ, where (τ1 + τ2 + ...) represents the magnitude of the total (net external) torque.

Question 112hard

For a rigid body rotating about a fixed z-axis, which of the following expressions correctly represents the component of its total angular momentum along the fixed axis (Lz)?

  1. Lz = mω
  2. Lz = Iω
  3. Lz = Iα
  4. Lz = r × p
Show answer

Answer: Lz = Iω

The angular momentum (L) of a rigid body is generally a vector quantity. However, for rotation about a fixed axis (say, the z-axis), the component of the total angular momentum along that axis (Lz) is directly proportional to the moment of inertia (I) about that axis and the angular velocity (ω). The relationship is given by Lz = Iω. This is analogous to linear momentum p = mv.

Question 113hard

A ballet dancer performing a pirouette brings her arms closer to her body. What happens to her angular speed and why?

  1. Angular speed decreases due to increased moment of inertia.
  2. Angular speed increases due to increased moment of inertia.
  3. Angular speed decreases due to decreased moment of inertia.
  4. Angular speed increases due to decreased moment of inertia.
Show answer

Answer: Angular speed increases due to decreased moment of inertia.

This phenomenon is an application of the conservation of angular momentum. When the dancer brings her arms closer to her body, her mass distribution shifts closer to the axis of rotation, thereby decreasing her moment of inertia (I). Since there are negligible external torques acting on her, her total angular momentum (L = Iω) remains constant. For L to remain constant, if I decreases, her angular speed (ω) must increase proportionally.

Question 114hard

If the moment of inertia of a rotating system decreases due to an internal change (e.g., a child folding arms on a rotating stool), how does its angular speed change to conserve angular momentum?

  1. Angular speed decreases proportionally.
  2. Angular speed increases proportionally.
  3. Angular speed remains constant.
  4. Angular speed changes unpredictably.
Show answer

Answer: Angular speed increases proportionally.

According to the principle of conservation of angular momentum, if no external torque acts on a system, its total angular momentum (L) remains constant. Angular momentum is given by L = Iω, where I is the moment of inertia and ω is the angular speed. If the moment of inertia (I) decreases, then for L to remain constant, the angular speed (ω) must increase proportionally.

Question 115hard

Under what condition does an ellipse simplify into a circle?

  1. When its semi-minor axis becomes zero.
  2. When its two foci merge into a single point.
  3. When its eccentricity becomes greater than 1.
  4. When its semi-major axis becomes infinitely large.
Show answer

Answer: When its two foci merge into a single point.

An ellipse is defined by two foci. A circle is a special case of an ellipse where the two foci coincide at a single point, which then becomes the center of the circle. In this scenario, the semi-major axis and semi-minor axis become equal, both representing the radius of the circle.

Question 116hard

When a point mass is situated outside a hollow spherical shell, what happens to the perpendicular components of the gravitational forces exerted by different regions of the shell?

  1. They add up to create a net force perpendicular to the line joining the point mass to the center.
  2. They cancel out, leaving only a resultant force along the line joining the point mass to the center.
  3. They are negligible and do not contribute to the total force.
  4. They cause the point mass to orbit the shell.
Show answer

Answer: They cancel out, leaving only a resultant force along the line joining the point mass to the center.

Due to the spherical symmetry of the shell, for any small region on the shell exerting a gravitational force on the point mass, there will be a symmetrically opposite region on the shell. The components of the gravitational forces from these regions that are perpendicular to the line joining the point mass to the center of the shell will cancel each other out. This leaves only the components along the line joining the point mass to the center, resulting in a net force directed towards the center of the shell.

Question 117hard

For small heights 'h' (where h << R_E), the approximate formula for the acceleration due to gravity, g(h), is given by:

  1. g(h) ≈ g(1 + h/R_E)
  2. g(h) ≈ g(1 - h/R_E)
  3. g(h) ≈ g(1 - 2h/R_E)
  4. g(h) ≈ g(1 + 2h/R_E)
Show answer

Answer: g(h) ≈ g(1 - 2h/R_E)

The acceleration due to gravity at a height h above the Earth's surface is given by g(h) = GM / (R_E + h)^2. For small heights (h << R_E), we can use the binomial approximation (1 + x)^n ≈ 1 + nx. So, g(h) = GM / [R_E^2 (1 + h/R_E)^2] = (GM/R_E^2) * (1 + h/R_E)^-2. Since g = GM/R_E^2, we have g(h) = g * (1 - 2h/R_E). Thus, the approximate formula is g(h) ≈ g(1 - 2h/R_E).

Question 118hard

How is the total gravitational potential energy of a system of multiple particles determined?

  1. By averaging the potential energies of all particles.
  2. By summing the gravitational potential energies for all possible distinct pairs of its constituent particles, applying the superposition principle.
  3. By multiplying the potential energies of all particles.
  4. By calculating the potential energy of the center of mass of the system.
Show answer

Answer: By summing the gravitational potential energies for all possible distinct pairs of its constituent particles, applying the superposition principle.

The total gravitational potential energy of a system of multiple particles is determined by summing the gravitational potential energies for all possible distinct pairs of its constituent particles. This is a direct application of the superposition principle, which states that the total potential energy is the algebraic sum of the potential energies due to individual pairs.

Question 119hard

Which of the following statements is true regarding gravitational force and gravitational potential energy?

  1. Gravitational force is a non-conservative force, and V = G(m1m2)/r.
  2. Gravitational force is a conservative force, and V = -G(m1m2)/r.
  3. Gravitational force is a conservative force, and V = G(m1m2)/r.
  4. Gravitational force is a non-conservative force, and V = -G(m1m2)/r.
Show answer

Answer: Gravitational force is a conservative force, and V = -G(m1m2)/r.

Gravitational force is a conservative force, meaning the work done by it is independent of the path taken. The gravitational potential energy V associated with two particles of masses m1 and m2 separated by a distance r is given by V = -G(m1m2)/r, where V is conventionally taken to be zero at r → ∞. The negative sign indicates that the force is attractive.

Question 120hard

If the zero of potential energy is taken at infinity, what is the total energy (E) of an orbiting satellite in a stable circular orbit in relation to its kinetic energy (K) and potential energy (U)?

  1. E = K
  2. E = U
  3. E = -K
  4. E = 2K
Show answer

Answer: E = -K

For an orbiting satellite in a stable circular orbit, the kinetic energy (K) is equal to half the magnitude of the potential energy (U), i.e., K = -U/2. The total mechanical energy (E) is the sum of kinetic and potential energy: E = K + U. Substituting U = -2K, we get E = K + (-2K) = -K. Alternatively, substituting K = -U/2, we get E = -U/2 + U = U/2. Therefore, the total energy is negative of its kinetic energy.

Question 121hard

Stress is defined as:

  1. The deforming force applied per unit area.
  2. The restoring force developed per unit area inside a body when subjected to a deforming force.
  3. The change in length per unit original length.
  4. The ratio of Young's modulus to strain.
Show answer

Answer: The restoring force developed per unit area inside a body when subjected to a deforming force.

Stress is defined as the restoring force developed per unit area inside a body when it is subjected to a deforming force. Mathematically, if F is the force applied normal to the cross-section and A is the area of the cross-section of the body, then stress = F/A. It is a measure of the internal forces that particles within a continuous material exert on each other.

Question 122hard

On a stress-strain curve, what does the yield point (B) and its corresponding stress (σy) signify?

  1. The point where the material breaks.
  2. The maximum stress a material can withstand without undergoing any deformation.
  3. The maximum stress a material can withstand without undergoing permanent deformation.
  4. The point where the material starts to behave elastically.
Show answer

Answer: The maximum stress a material can withstand without undergoing permanent deformation.

The point B on a stress-strain curve is known as the yield point (or elastic limit). The stress corresponding to this point is called the yield strength (σy) of the material. It signifies the maximum stress a material can withstand without undergoing permanent deformation. Beyond this point, the material starts to deform plastically, meaning it will not return to its original shape once the deforming force is removed.

Question 123hard

A performer applies a load of 1078 N on each thighbone. If the length of the thighbone is 0.5 m, Young's modulus for bone is 9.4 × 10^9 N m^-2, and its cross-sectional area is 1.26 × 10^-3 m^2, what is the compression in each thighbone?

  1. 4.55 × 10^-4 m
  2. 4.55 × 10^-5 m
  3. 5.39 × 10^-5 m
  4. 5.39 × 10^-4 m
Show answer

Answer: 4.55 × 10^-5 m

We use the formula for elongation (ΔL) due to stress: ΔL = (F × L) / (Y × A). Given: F = 1078 N, L = 0.5 m, Y = 9.4 × 10^9 N m^-2, A = 1.26 × 10^-3 m^2. ΔL = (1078 × 0.5) / (9.4 × 10^9 × 1.26 × 10^-3) ΔL = 539 / (11.844 × 10^6) ΔL ≈ 4.55 × 10^-5 m.

Question 124hard

The work done in stretching a wire of original length L and cross-section A by an elongation 'l' is given by:

  1. W = (1/2) (YAl/L)
  2. W = (YAl^2/L)
  3. W = (1/2) (YAl^2/L)
  4. W = (YAl/2L)
Show answer

Answer: W = (1/2) (YAl^2/L)

When a wire is stretched, the deforming force F is not constant but increases with elongation. For an infinitesimal elongation dl, the work done dW = F × dl. From Young's modulus, Y = (F/A) / (l/L), so F = (YAl/L). Substituting this into dW, we get dW = (YAl/L) dl. To find the total work done (W) for an elongation from 0 to l, we integrate: W = ∫₀ˡ (YAl/L) dl = (YA/L) ∫₀ˡ l dl = (YA/L) [l^2/2]₀ˡ = (1/2) (YAl^2/L).

Answer: Mechanical wave

Question 307easy

What is the speed of light in a medium with a refractive index of 1.5?

  1. 2 x 10^8 m/s
  2. 2.5 x 10^8 m/s
  3. 1.5 x 10^8 m/s
  4. 1 x 10^8 m/s
Show answer

Answer: 2.5 x 10^8 m/s

The speed of light in a medium is given by v = c / n, where c is the speed of light in vacuum and n is the refractive index. For n = 1.5, v = (3 x 10^8) / 1.5 = 2 x 10^8 m/s.

Question 319easy

What type of energy is associated with the motion of a 5 kg object moving at 2 m/s?

  1. Potential energy
  2. Thermal energy
  3. Electrical energy
  4. Kinetic energy
Show answer

Answer: Kinetic energy

Kinetic energy is the energy an object possesses due to its motion. It is calculated using the formula KE = 0.5 * m * v^2, where m is the mass and v is the velocity of the object.

Question 322easy

What is the term for the force that opposes motion between two rough surfaces in contact with a coefficient of friction of 0.5?

  3. Magnetic force
  4. Frictional force
Show answer

Answer: Frictional force

Question 355easy

What is the minimum velocity a 5 kg object must have to escape the gravitational pull of a planet with a mass of 6.0 x 10^24 kg and a radius of 6000 km?

  1. 8 km/s
  2. 10 km/s
  3. 12 km/s
  4. 15 km/s
Show answer

Answer: 12 km/s

To escape the gravitational pull, the object must have a velocity greater than or equal to the escape velocity, which is calculated using the formula v = sqrt(2GM/r), where G is the gravitational constant, M is the mass of the planet, and r is the radius of the planet.

Show answer

Answer: Acceleration

Acceleration is the process by which an object's velocity changes due to a net force, which applies to the rocket's velocity increase from 1000 m/s to 2000 m/s.

Answer: Biot-Savart Law

The Biot-Savart Law describes the process by which an electric current generates a magnetic field. The flux density of the magnetic field is proportional to the current.

  4. Evaporation

Answer: Convection

Answer: Erwin Schrodinger

Fluid friction occurs when an object is moving through a fluid, such as air or water, and it is also known as drag.
